Jamison Brereton

32 (652)
Indra
Medh─Бtithi K─Бс╣Зva
30 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged for the most part in trcas ╠е
The hymn begins with a call to the Kaс╣Зva poets to praise IndraтАЩs great deeds, and the next two verses (2тАУ3) provide a quick catalogue of IndraтАЩs victories over several of his lesser known opponents. This theme, with some of the same names/epithets, returns at the end of the hymn (esp. vss. 25тАУ27). In between we find the usual twin exhortations to IndraтАФto come to our soma sacrifice (rather than that of others; see esp. vss. 21тАУ22) and to give us wealth and aid. The reciprocal obligation of the sacrificers and the recipient of sacrifice is nicely expressed in verse 16, where IndraтАЩs debt to (other) sacrificers has been discharged by his countergift.
There is nothing of particular note in this hymn, though it is nicely executed. It also contains several hapaxes and words with apparently non-Indo-Aryan phonol ogy, especially toward the beginning, that give it a slightly exotic air.
The internal structure of the hymn is not entirely clear. We follow OldenbergтАЩs analysis, whereby the hymn consists of tr╠еcas plus a final verse (30) save for verses 19тАУ20, which form an incomplete tr╠еca with perhaps a verse missing. However, the tr╠еcas thus identified show little internal unity.1094 VIII.32

English translation:

тАЬCelebrate with songs the great deeds of Indra, the drinker of the stale Soma, when in his exhilaration.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Kaс╣Зvas, with a song proclaim (the deeds) of Indra of the silvery drink
done in the exhilaration of soma,

Griffith

KANVAS, tell forth with song the deeds of Indra, the Impetuous,
Wrought in the Soma’s wild delight.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe fierce (deity) who, liberating the waters, has slain Sс╣Ыbinda, Anar┼Ыani, Pipru, D─Бsa and Ahi┼Ыuva.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The slave: d─Бsa = a proper name; d─Бsam ca ahi┼Ыuvam ca

Jamison Brereton

Who smashed Sr╠еbinda (so he became) harmless, smashed Pipru the D─Бsa puffed up like a snake [/Ah─л┼Ыuva]тАФ
he the strong one letting flow the waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes ├бnar┼Ыanim and ah─л┼Ы├║vam as PNs, in addition to sс╣Ы╠Бbindum and the familiar p├нprum. Mayrhofer (2003, Personennamen) is uncertain about ├бnar┼Ыani-.

Scarlatta (538-39) tr. all as PNs as well, but discusses the possible interpretations of ah─л┼Ы┼л╠Б-. On the basis of the parallel he cites in IV.16.13 p├нprum mс╣Ы╠Бgayaс╣Г ┼Ы┼л┼Ыuv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam тАЬPipru Mrgaya, ╠е swollen with power,тАЭ with the pf. part. to тИЪ┼Ы┼л, I prefer to take ah─л┼Ы┼л╠Б- as a meaningful epithet. The question is then what the first member ah─л- represents.

Although it would be easier to identify it with ah─л╠Б- тАШfertile cowтАЩ, which matches it exactly, I prefer to take it as a metrically lengthened version of ├бhi- тАШsnakeтАЩ, which makes more sense in the designation of a demon. See Scarlatta (loc. cit.), also EWA s.v. ah─л╠Б-. All four occurrences of this stem would have four short syllables if the second werenтАЩt long ─л, but I do not otherwise have an explanation of the lengthening. But note pr─Б┼Ы┼л╠Б- below (16b) with the same lengthening before ┼Ы┼л╠Б-.

As for ├бnar┼Ыani- I would again prefer to give it full lexical value, relating it (as Grassmann does) to ├бnar┼Ыa-r─Бti- (VIII.99.4) тАШpossessing non-harmful giftsтАЩ(?), ar┼Ыas─Бn├бdesignation of another demon. See EWA s.v. ar┼Ыas─Бn├б-. However, the root etymology (supposed тИЪar┼Ы/с╣Ы┼Ы тАШharmтАЩ) is not strong, and the analysis remains uncertain. If it does mean тАШharmlessтАЩ, the adjective is used proleptically, as is not uncommon.

The name of the first demon, Sс╣Ыbindu, displays non-Indo-Aryan phonology.

See Kuiper (Aryans 40-41).

Griffith

Strong God, he slew Anarsani, Srbinda, Pipru, and the fiend,
Ahisuva, and loosed the floods.

Geldner

Der den Sribinda, den Anarsani, den Pipru, den Dasa Ahisu erschlug, der gewaltige, der die Gew├дsser laufen lie├Я!

Grassmann

Des starken, der Sribindha schlug Anar├зani, Ahi├зuva, Den Unhold Pipru, Flut ergoss.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬI invoke the victorious handsome-jawed Indra for your protection, and to hear (your praises), as (atraveller invokes) the water from the cloud.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Water from the cloud: t┼лrс╣З─Б┼Ыam na girer adhi: t┼лrс╣З─Б┼Ыa =udaka (t┼лrс╣З─Б┼Ыamudakam bhavati t┼лrс╣Зama┼Ыnute : Nirukta 5.16); as a man in hot weather calls for water fromthe cloud, yath─Б gharmebhitptaс╕е pum─Бn udakam megham prati hvayati

Jamison Brereton

To the famed one (bring) your (soma) boldly, like a torrent [?] from the mountain.
I invoke him of good lips for help.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner I supply both тАЬbringтАЭ and тАЬsoma,тАЭ though I would prefer to have more formulaic or textual support for providing this extraneous material - however, cf. II.14.8 g├бbhistip┼лtam bharata ┼Ыrut─Б╠Бya тАЬBring what is purified by your hand [=soma] to the one who is famed,тАЭ adduced by Geldner The preverb pr├бti occurs with тИЪbhс╣Ы (see, e.g., VIII.20.9 pr├бti тАж ┼Ы├бrdh─Бya m─Б╠Бrut─Бya bharadhvam / havy─Б╠БтАж), but is not common.

t┼л╠Бrс╣З─Б┼Ыa- is a hapax without etymology (though OldenbergтАЩs literal gloss, тАЬwas dem Ueberschreitenden Verschwinden, Untergang bringt,тАЭ implies тИЪtс╣Э and тИЪna┼Ы, without attempting to explain the morphology). I follow the consensus, that the word refers to a watercourse of some sort, since that makes sense in context. As often, verbal play may have had a role in its appearance here: 4b #t┼л╠Бrс╣З─Б┼Ыaс╣Г n├б … is partly echoed by 5c p├║raс╣Г n├б ┼Ы┼лra тАж (┼лr/ur na am ┼Ы, though not in the same order in both).

Down like a torrent from the hill.

Bringet dem ber├╝hmten Indra euren Soma getrost dar wie einen Gie├Яbach vom Berge: Ich rufe den Sch├╢nlippigen zum Beistand.

English translation:

тАЬIf you are propitiated by my libation and praise, and bestow food (upon me), come with viands from afar.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

If you will take pleasure in my pressed (soma) or you will find delight in my solemn speech,
from afar come near through your own power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

An alternative syntactic analysis of ab would take everything through v─Б in b as part of the y├бdi clause with r─Бr├бс╣Зaс╕е as verb, and start the main clause with d├бdhase, accented because itтАЩs clause-initial: тАЬIf you will take pleasure in my pressed (soma) or in my solemn speech, you will find delight.тАЭ There are no strong arguments either way.

If my libation gladdens, if thou takest pleasure in my laud,
Come with thy Godhead from afar.

Wenn du an meinem Safte Freude hast oder an dem Loblied gefallen findest, so komm doch nach Belieben aus der Ferne her!

Grassmann

Wenn du an meinem Trank dich freust, an meinem Spruch Gefallen hast, So komm mit Lust von ferne her.

тАЬGratified by us, bring us undiminished food, Maghavan, for vast is your wealth.тАЭ

And bring us food, granting it inexhaustibleтАФ
many are your goods, liberal oneтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand GeldnerтАЩs tr. of saс╣Гrar─Бс╣З├бс╕е as тАШmitteilsamтАЩ (communicative, talkative) and as if it were an adjective modifying food (тАЬbring us mitteilsam SpeiseтАжтАЭ). (I assume that the specialization of this German cmpd for [verbal] communication postdates GeldnerтАЩs language acquisition stage and his usage reflects some sense of teilen тАШdivide, shareтАЩ.) K├╝mmel (421) suggests that this participle means тАЬbereitwillig, spendefreudig,тАЭ implying that it is used absolutely and doesnтАЩt take an object. This certainly is possible here, but doesnтАЩt bring us to GeldnerтАЩs rendering.

In any case, the form here (-rar─Бс╣З├бс╕е to тИЪr─Б) echoes r─Бr├бс╣Зaс╕е (to тИЪran) in 6a.

Great is thy wealth, O Maghavan.

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke Indra, who is greatly to be praised, whose arm is stretched out for the protection (of theworld), acting nobly for our defence.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We invoke him of stammering speech, of stout forearms,
for help;
(we invoke) him who creates success, for aid.

Jamison Brereton Notes

bс╣Ыb├бduktha- is a hapax and has aggressively non-Indo-Aryan phonology (not one, but two bтАЩs). My rendering is adopted from Weber (1891, cited by EWA s.v. bс╣Ыb├║-; see also s.v. bс╣Ыb├бduktha-). The word must deliberately evoke the name and epithet bс╣Ыh├бd-uktha- but should not be emended thereto; see Oldenberg and Geldner If WeberтАЩs suggestion is correct, this may be a little joke, implying that Indra is powerful but not very good with words.

Griffith

Let us call him to aid whose hands stretch far, to whom high laud is due.
Who worketh well to succour us.

Geldner

Wir rufen den Indra mit langen Armen zum Beistand, ihn, der das Rechte tut, zur Hilfe.

Grassmann

Den hochgelobten rufen wir, der weit den Arm zur H├╝lfe streckt, Den segenwirkenden zum Schutz.

Elizarenkova

A novel construction, at least as interpreted by Geldner (fld. by Klein and accepted also by me). The word -kratu- тАШintention, resolveтАЩ is extracted from IndraтАЩs epithet ┼Ыat├б-kratu- and implicitly made object of kс╣Ыn├│ti, represented by the enclitic pronoun ─лm. Jamison Brereton

He as тАЬable oneтАЭ will be able for us, he who has gifts and brings them nearтАФ
Indra, with all his help.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A similar type of construction as the immediately preceding verse, though the connection between epithet and its dynamic manifestation is clearer: the epithet ┼Ыakr├бс╕е тАШableтАЩ is transformed into the verb ┼Ыakat тАШhe will be ableтАЩ. For an almost identical construction see I.10.6 and discussion there.

In both 11 and 12 I take cid as marking the epithet to be transformed, though in 11a it is displaced to the left.

Geldner interprets the hapax antar─Бbhar├б- as тАЬder zwischen den K├дmpfen steht,тАЭ presuming an analysis antar─Б-bhar├б-, rejected by Oldenberg, who favors the Pp antara─Бbhar├б-. This fits the context better.

Er, welcher stark ist, sei zur Hand, der gabenreiche, schenkende, Mit allen H├╝lfen Indra uns.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHim who comes near, the mighty, the firm in battles, the acquirer of fame, the lord of vast riches throughhis prowess.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Fame: ┼Ыravojitam = the winner of wealth or food

Jamison Brereton

The guider, the very steadfast one who wins fame in battles,
lord over much by his strength.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes m├бhi sthir├бm as the neut. obj. of ─Бyant─Б╠Бram, supplying тАШbowтАЩ: тАЬDer den grossen starken (Bogen) spannt.тАЭ There are several objections to this. First, itтАЩs ─Б╠БтИЪtan, not ─Б╠БтИЪyam, that is the standard idiom for stretching or spanning the bow, including in the passages he cites as parallels. Moreover, suffix-accented -t├бr- stems (like ─Б╠Бyant├бr- here) ordinarily govern the genitive not the accusative, and although this rule is often violated, the fact that niyant├бr- in the following verse (15), an agent noun to the same root, does take the genitive makes it less likely that this one would take an accusative. I therefore take sthir├бm as a modifier of Indra (as in the next hymn, VIII.33.9, and elsewhere) and m├бhi as adverbial. ─Бyant├бr- here is best interpreted in the context of ─Б╠Бyachantu in 23b below.

Griffith

Who bringeth what is great and firm, who winneth glory in his wars,
Lord of vast wealth through power and might.

Geldner

Der den gro├Яen starken Bogen spannt, in den K├дmpfen Ruhm gewinnt, ├╝ber vieles Macht hat durch seine St├дrke.

Grassmann

Der grosses, starkes Gut ertheilt und in den Schlachten Ruhm erwirbt, der ├╝ber vieles m├дchtig herrscht.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVerily no debt is due (to the gods) by those Soma-partaking br─Бhmaс╣Зas offering libations; the Soma isnot drunk without the expenditure of boundless (wealth).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Verily no debt is due: he who has a son, or is chaste, isfree from debt, i.e., to the gods and manes: eс╣гa v─Б anс╣Ыс╣Зo yaс╕е putr─л yajv─Б brahmac─Бriv─Бs─л: Taittir─лyaSaс╣Гhit─Б 6.3.10.5; without the expendiure of boundless wealth: aprat─Б = avist─лrс╣Зadhanena, by one who hasnot abundant wealth

Jamison Brereton

There exists no debt to the formulators, nor to the puffed-up pressers now: no soma has been drunk without a counter(gift).

Jamison Brereton Notes

On pr─Б┼Ы┼л╠Б- see Scarlatta (539-40) and vs. 2 above, as well as comm. ad VIII.31.6.

This verse is oddly couched as an impersonal. GeldnerтАЩs interpretation of it is conventional: the humans have fulfilled their obligation (с╣Ыс╣З├бm) to the god and he correspondingly fulfills his to them. But the curiously detached affect of the expression gives me pause, and the temporal relations between ab and c are backwards for this interpretation: n┼лn├бm тАШnowтАЩ situates the first two p─Бdas temporally after the action of the third, whose verb is the perfect pape, and the perfect of тИЪp─Б is generally preterital. I therefore interpret the verse quite differently from Geldner I take the debt to be IndraтАЩs, what he owes to the human worshippers who praise and press soma for him. But he has preemptatively fulfilled it: his somadrinking is always accompanied by his gift. The reason for the indirect and impersonal expression is to avoid saying directly that Indra could owe a debt to humans. This interpretation requires taking the genitives in ab as quasi-datives, but this is quite common.

On aprat─Б╠Бsee Oldenberg

Griffith

No debt is due by Brahmans now, by active men who press the juice:
Well hath each Soma-draught been paid.

Geldner

Nicht besteht jetzt eine Schuld der p├╝nktlichen somapressenden Priester, nicht ward der Soma ohne Gegenleistung getrunken.

Grassmann

Nicht wirken falsch die Beter jetzt, noch auch die schnellen Kelterer, Nicht ist umsonst des Soma’s Trunk.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSing praises to the adorable (Indra), repeat prayers to the adorable (Indra), address hymns to theadorable (Indra).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Sing just to the admirable one, to the admirable one recite
solemn words;
perform sacred formulations just for the admirable one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The loc. p├бnye as beneficiary/target of the verbs тИЪg─Б тАШsingтАЩ and тИЪ┼Ыaс╣Гs тАШreciteтАЩ is peculiar: these verbs generally take the dative or, esp. with certain preverbs, the accusative. But loc. p├бnya in sandhi matches the nominative p├бnya in sandhi (that is, underlying p├бnyaс╕е) that begins the next verse (18a), and this match accounts for the unusual case usage. A small, but telling, example of how rhetorical motivations can override strictly grammatical issues.

Den wahrhaft herrlichen besingt und sagt ihm eure Spr├╝che auf, Gebete bringt dem herrlichen.

English translation:

тАЬThe powerful Indra, the discomfiter of hundreds and thousands, unchecked (by foes), is adorable; hewho is the benefactor of the sacrificer.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The admirable one will tear out hundreds, thousands (of goods)тАФhe the unobstructable prizewinner,
Indra, who is the strengthener of him who offers sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The intensive (that is, iterative-frequentative) dardirat is appropriate to the multiple objects implied.

May be, unchecked, strong, meet for praise, bring hundreds, thousands forth to light,
Indra who aids the worshipper.

English translation:

тАЬDrink of the (Soma) purchased by the cow, that (Soma) which is mixed with water, that by which, Indra,is especially yours.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Purchased by the cow: svadhainav─Бn─Бm dhenv─Б kс╣Ыt─Бn som─Бn = dhenv─Б kr─лс╣З─Бti:Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 6.1.10.2

Jamison Brereton

Drink of (the pressings) that have their own milk-cows, both (the pressing) at the son of TugraтАЩs [=Bhujyu]
and this one right here, which is yours, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The curious term sv├бdhainava- appears to mean тАШhaving its own milk/milk-cowsтАЩ, with vс╣Ыddhi of dhen├║- (see AiG II.2.114). It echoes svadh─Б╠Б├бnu in 19a, and, as often, this echo may help account for its deployment here. Its referent is presumably soma-pressings or soma-drinks.

The relation between p─Бda a and the relative clauses of bc is, at best, тАЬimproper.тАЭ That is, the two singular forms y├бс╕е in b and c must have as their (rough) antecedent the gen. plural of p─Бda a referring to the pressings/drinks.

English translation:

тАЬIndra, who has beheld our praises, proceed in three directions from a distance, pass beyond the fiveorders of beings.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Three directions: i.e., coming to us from in front, from behind and from the side

Jamison Brereton

Pass through the three distant realms; pass over the five peoples, keeping watch over the nourishing streams, o Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take ├бti only with b: Indra is not supposed to pass over the three realms, but through them on his way to us. It is only the (other) peoples he is to pass over.

English translation:

тАЬAs the sun disperses his rays, do you disperse (wealth upon me); may my praises rapidly draw you, aswaters (reach) the low ground.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like the sun its ray, let loose your rein. Let my hymns guide
you here
like waters, converging, to the deep.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a plays on the ambiguity of ra┼Ыm├н-, both тАШrayтАЩ and тАШreinтАЩ.

Although the simile in c seems to match the frame in b in case (nom. g├нraс╕е / ─Б╠Бpaс╕е, acc. tv─Б / nimn├бm), there is a functional mismatch: the waters are not guiding the deep as the songs are guiding Indra. It therefore seems best to take ─Б╠Бpaс╕е as one of the occasional examples of nom. for acc. in this stem, corresponding to tv─Б in the frame, with nimn├бm a further specification of goal. Geldner clearly recognizes the problem and supplies a verb for the simile in c, тАЬwie die Gew├дsser тАж (fliessen),тАЭ but this violates the structure of the RVic simile, which always holds the verb in common with the frame.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAdhvaryu, quickly pour forth the Soma to the hero Indra with the goodly jaws; bring the Soma for hisdrinking.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Adhvaryu! Pour out the soma for the belipped hero.
Bring of the pressing (for him) to drink.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The h├н in the first imperative clause provides the logical basis for the second one. See Brereton 2012.

Griffith

Now to the Hero fair of cheek, Adhvaryu, pour the Soma forth:
Bring of the juice that he may drink

Geldner

Adhvaryu! So schenk doch f├╝r den Helden mit ge├╢ffneten Lippen den Soma ein; trag ihm vom Safte auf zum Trunke!

Grassmann

Auf, Priester, giesse Soma zu dem Mann, der schon die Lippen spitzt, Und reich den Saft zum Trunk ihm dar.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWho clove the cloud for (the issue of) the rain, who sent down the waters, who plural ced the mature (milk)in the cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who split the bolt of the water and released the rivers
downward,
who fixed the cooked (milk) fast in the cows,

Griffith

Who cleft the water-cloud in twain, loosed rivers for their downward flow,
And set the ripe milk in the kine.

Der des Wassers R├дuber zerspaltete, die Fl├╝sse abw├дrts laufen lie├Я, der in den K├╝hen die gekochte Milch festlegt.

Er, der des Wassers Stall erbrach, herab die Str├╢me rinnen liess Und gare Milch den K├╝hen gab,

English translation:

тАЬThe brilliant Indra slew Vс╣Ыtra, Aurс╣Зav─Бbha, Ahi┼Ыava; he smote Arbuda with frost.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Indra: с╣Ыc─лс╣гama =с╣Ыc─Б d─лpty─Б sama indraс╕е

Jamison Brereton

He who is equal to song smashed Vr╠еtra, (smashed) the spiderтАЩs son [/Aurс╣Зav─Бbha] and the one puffed up like a
snake [/Ah─л┼Ыuva].
With snow [/an icicle?] he pierced Arbuda.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On с╣Ы╠Бc─лс╣гama- see I.61.1.

As in 2b ah─л┼Ы├║vam may be a PN, but I prefer to take it with lexical value. The same problem is encountered with aurс╣Зav─Бbh├б-. Arbuda, however, is a known enemy of Indra, but this episode, with snow as the weapon, is otherwise unknown.

Note again the non-Indo-─Аryan phonology.

The return of the theme of IndraтАЩs smashing named enemies from vs. 2 suggests a ring, and the fact that the following verses (27-28) sketch a ring with vs. 1 strengthens this impression.

Griffith

He, meet for praise, slew Vrtra, slew Ahisuva, Urnavabha’s son,
And pierced th:rough Arbuda with frost.

Geldner

Der …….. erschlug den Vritra, den Aurnavabha, den Ahisu. Mit Schnee bewarf er den Arbuda.

Grassmann

Er schlug den Vritra glanzdurchstrahlt, die Spinnenbrut Ahi├зuva, Durch Frost vertilgt’ er Arbuda.
